<!-- {"role": "assistant", "content": "I'll implement window functions for KosDB v3.3.0. Let me start by creating the window_functions.py module:  <CreateFile>\n<fileName>window_functions.py</fileName>\n<contentOfFile>\"\"\"\nWindow Functions Module for KosDB v3.3.0\n\nProvides SQL window functions:\n- ROW_NUMBER(): Sequential row number\n- RANK(): Rank with gaps\n- DENSE_RANK(): Rank without gaps\n- LEAD(): Access next row\n- LAG(): Access previous row\n- FIRST_VALUE(): First value in window\n- LAST_VALUE(): Last value in window\n\nSupports OVER clause with PARTITION BY and ORDER BY.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom typing import List, Dict, Any, Optional, Callable\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass\nfrom enum import Enum\n\n\nclass WindowFunctionType(Enum):\n    \"\"\"Types of window functions.\"\"\"\n    ROW_NUMBER = \"ROW_NUMBER\"\n    RANK = \"RANK\"\n    DENSE_RANK = \"DENSE_RANK\"\n    LEAD = \"LEAD\"\n    LAG = \"LAG\"\n    FIRST_VALUE = \"FIRST_VALUE\"\n    LAST_VALUE = \"LAST_VALUE\"\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass WindowFrame:\n    \"\"\"Window frame specification.\"\"\"\n    partition_by: Optional[List[str]] = None\n    order_by: Optional[List[tuple]] = None  # [(column, direction), ...]\n    frame_type: Optional[str] = None  # ROWS, RANGE\n    start_bound: Optional[str] = None  # UNBOUNDED PRECEDING, N PRECEDING, CURRENT ROW\n    end_bound: Optional[str] = None  # CURRENT ROW, N FOLLOWING, UNBOUNDED FOLLOWING\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass WindowFunctionCall:\n    \"\"\"Window function call specification.\"\"\"\n    function_type: WindowFunctionType\n    args: List[Any]  # For LEAD/LAG: [column, offset, default]\n    window_frame: WindowFrame\n    alias: Optional[str] = None\n\n\nclass WindowFunctionExecutor:\n    \"\"\"\n    Executor for window functions.\n    \n    Processes data row by row and computes window function results.\n    \"\"\"\n    \n    def __init__(self):\n        self.functions = {\n            WindowFunctionType.ROW_NUMBER: self._row_number,\n            WindowFunctionType.RANK: self._rank,\n            WindowFunctionType.DENSE_RANK: self._dense_rank,\n            WindowFunctionType.LEAD: self._lead,\n            WindowFunctionType.LAG: self._lag,\n            WindowFunctionType.FIRST_VALUE: self._first_value,\n            WindowFunctionType.LAST_VALUE: self._last_value,\n        }\n    \n    def execute(self, data: List[Dict], window_calls: List[WindowFunctionCall]) -> List[Dict]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Execute window functions on data.\n        \n        Args:\n            data: List of row dictionaries\n            window_calls: List of window function calls\n        \n        Returns:\n            Data with window function results added\n        \"\"\"\n        if not data:\n            return data\n        \n        result = []\n        \n        for call in window_calls:\n            data = self._execute_single_function(data, call)\n        \n        return data\n    \n    def _execute_single_function(self, data: List[Dict], call: WindowFunctionCall) -> List[Dict]:\n        \"\"\"Execute a single window function.\"\"\"\n        func = self.functions.get(call.function_type)\n        if not func:\n            raise ValueError(f\"Unknown window function: {call.function_type}\")\n        \n        return func(data, call)\n    \n    def _partition_data(self, data: List[Dict], partition_cols: Optional[List[str]]) -> Dict[tuple, List[Dict]]:\n        \"\"\"Partition data by specified columns.\"\"\"\n        if not partition_cols:\n            return {(): data}\n        \n        partitions = {}\n        for row in data:\n            key = tuple(row.get(col) for col in partition_cols)\n            if key not in partitions:\n                partitions[key] = []\n            partitions[key].append(row)\n        \n        return partitions\n    \n    def _sort_partition(self, partition: List[Dict], order_by: Optional[List[tuple]]) -> List[Dict]:\n        \"\"\"Sort partition by ORDER BY clause.\"\"\"\n        if not order_by:\n            return partition\n        \n        def sort_key(row):\n            keys = []\n            for col, direction in order_by:\n                val = row.get(col)\n                # Handle None values\n                if val is None:\n                    keys.append((1, None))  # None sorts last\n                else:\n                    keys.append((0, val))\n            return keys\n        \n        reverse = any(direction.upper() == 'DESC' for _, direction in order_by)\n        return sorted(partition, key=sort_key, reverse=reverse)\n    \n    def _row_number(self, data: List[Dict], call: WindowFunctionCall) -> List[Dict]:\n        \"\"\"Compute ROW_NUMBER().\"\"\"\n        result = []\n        partitions = self._partition_data(data, call.window_frame.partition_by)\n        \n        for key, partition in partitions.items():\n            sorted_partition = self._sort_partition(partition, call.window_frame.order_by)\n            \n            for i, row in enumerate(sorted_partition, 1):\n                new_row = row.copy()\n                alias = call.alias or f\"row_number_{call.function_type.value.lower()}\"\n                new_row[alias] = i\n                result.append(new_row)\n        \n        return result\n    \n    def _rank(self, data: List[Dict], call: WindowFunctionCall) -> List[Dict]:\n        \"\"\"Compute RANK() with gaps.\"\"\"\n        result = []\n        partitions = self._partition_data(data, call.window_frame.partition_by)\n        \n        for key, partition in partitions.items():\n            sorted_partition = self._sort_partition(partition, call.window_frame.order_by)\n            \n            rank = 1\n            prev_key = None\n            \n            for i, row in <!-- {"role": "assistant", "content": "Now let me add window function parsing support to the _parse_select_columns method:  <ReplaceLine>\n<fileName>parser.py</fileName>\n<fromLine>270</fromLine>\n<toLine>300</toLine>\n<replacement>    def _parse_select_columns(self, columns_str: str) -> List[Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse SELECT column list with JSON extraction and window function support.\"\"\"\n        columns = []\n        parts = self._split_columns(columns_str)\n        \n        for part in parts:\n            part = part.strip()\n            if not part:\n                continue\n            \n            # Check for window functions: FUNC(args) OVER (...)\n            window_match = re.match(r'(\\w+)\\s*\\(([^)]*)\\)\\s+OVER\\s*\\(([^)]+)\\)(?:\\s+AS\\s+(\\w+))?', part, re.IGNORECASE)\n            if window_match:\n                func_name = window_match.group(1).upper()\n                args = window_match.group(2).strip()\n                over_clause = window_match.group(3).strip()\n                alias = window_match.group(4)\n                \n                columns.append({\n                    'type': 'WINDOW_FUNCTION',\n                    'function': func_name,\n                    'args': [a.strip() for a in args.split(',')] if args else [],\n                    'over': self._parse_over_clause(over_clause),\n                    'alias': alias or f\"{func_name.lower()}_result\"\n                })\n                continue\n            \n            # \n    def test_lead(self):\n        \"\"\"Test LEAD() execution.\"\"\"\n        call = WindowFunctionCall(\n            function_type=WindowFunctionType.LEAD,\n            args=['salary', '1', '0'],\n TestWindowFunctionExecution(unittest.TestCase):\n    \"\"\"Test window function execution.\"\"\"\n    \n    def setUp(self):\n        self.executor = WindowFunctionExecutor()\n        \n        # Sample data\n        self.sample_data = [\n            {'dept': 'Sales', 'name': 'Alice', 'salary': 50000, 'hire_date': '2020-01-15'},\n            {'dept': 'Sales', 'name': 'Bob', 'salary': 55000, 'hire_date': '2019-03-20'},\n            {'dept': 'Sales', 'name': 'Carol', 'salary': 55000, 'hire_date': '2018-06-10'},\n            {'dept': 'IT', 'name': 'David', 'salary': 60000, 'hire_date': '2017-11-05'},\n            {'dept': 'IT', 'name': 'Eve', 'salary': 65000, 'hire_date': '2016-08-15'},\n        ]\n    \n    def test_row_number(self):\n        \"\"\"Test ROW_NUMBER() execution.\"\"\"\n        call = WindowFunctionCall(\n            function_type=WindowFunctionType.ROW_NUMBER,\n            args=[],\n            window_frame=WindowFrame(partition_by=['dept'], order_by=[('salary', 'DESC')]),\n            alias='row_num'\n        )\n        \n        result = self.executor.execute(self.sample_data.copy(), [call])\n        \n        # Check row numbers within each partition\n        sales_rows = [r for r in result if r['dept'] == 'Sales']\n        self.assertEqual(sales_rows[0]['row_num'], 1)\n        self.assertEqual(sales_rows[1]['row_num'], 2)\n        self.assertEqual(sales_rows[2]['row_num'], 3)\n    \n    def test_rank(self):\n        \"\"\"Test RANK() execution.\"\"\"\n        call = WindowFunctionCall(\n            function_type=WindowFunctionType.RANK,\n            args=[],\n            window_frame=WindowFrame(partition_by=['dept'], order_by=[('salary', 'DESC')]),\n            alias='rank'\n        )\n        \n        result = self.executor.execute(self.sample_data.copy(), [call])\n        \n        # Check ranks - should have gaps for ties\n        sales_rows = [r for r in result if r['dept'] == 'Sales']\n        # Carol and Bob have same salary (55000), so they should both rank 1\n        # Alice has 50000, should rank 3 (gap after 2)\n        ranks = [r['rank'] for r in sales_rows]\n        self.assertIn(1, ranks)\n        self.assertIn(3, ranks)\n    \n    def test_dense_rank(self):\n        \"\"\"Test DENSE_RANK() execution.\"\"\"\n        call = WindowFunctionCall(\n            function_type=WindowFunctionType.DENSE_RANK,\n            args=[],\n            window_frame=WindowFrame(partition_by=['dept'], order_by=[('salary', 'DESC')]),\n            alias='dense_rank'\n        )\n        \n        result = self.executor.execute(self.sample_data.copy(), [call])\n        \n        # Check dense ranks - no gaps for ties\n        sales_rows = [r for r in result if r['dept'] == 'Sales']\n        # Carol and Bob tie for rank 1, Alice is rank 2 (no gap)\n        ranks = [r['dense_rank'] for r in sales_rows]\n        self.assertIn(1, ranks)\n        self.assertIn(2, ranks)\n    \n    def test_lead(self):\n        \"\"\"Test LEAD() execution.\"\"\"\n        call = WindowFunctionCall(\n            function_type=WindowFunctionType.LEAD,\n            args=['salary', '1', '0'],\n            window_frame=WindowFrame(partition_by=['dept'], order_by=[('hire_date', 'ASC')]),\n            alias='next_salary'\n        )\n        \n        result = self.executor.execute(self.sample_data.copy(), [call])\n        \n        # Check LEAD values\n        sales_rows = sorted([r for r in result if r['dept'] == 'Sales'], \n                          key=lambda x: x['hire_date'])\n        # Carol (oldest) should see Bob's salary as next\n        self.assertEqual(sales_rows[0]['next_salary'], 55000)  # Carol sees Bob\n        # Bob should see Alice's salary\n        self.assertEqual(sales_rows[1]['next_salary'], 50000)  # Bob sees Alice\n        # Alice (newest) should see default (0)\n        self.assertEqual(sales_rows[2]['next_salary'], 0)\n    \n    def test_lag(self):\n        \"\"\"Test LAG() execution.\"\"\"\n        call = WindowFunctionCall(\n            function_type=WindowFunctionType.LAG,\n            args=['salary', '1', '0'],\n            window_frame=WindowFrame(partition_by=['dept'], order_by=[('hire_date', 'ASC')]),\n            alias='prev_salary'\n        )\n        \n        result = self.executor.execute(self.sample_data.copy(), [call])\n        \n        # Check LAG values\n        sales_rows = sorted([r for r in result if r['dept'] == 'Sales'], \n                          key=lambda x: x['hire_date'])\n        # Carol (oldest) should see default (0)\n        self.assertEqual(sales_rows[0]['prev_salary'], 0)\n        # Bob should see Carol's salary\n        self.assertEqual(sales_rows[1]['prev_salary'], 55000)\n        # Alice should see Bob's salary\n        self.assertEqual(sales_rows[2]['prev_salary'], 55000)\n    \n    def test_first_value(self):\n        \"\"\"Test FIRST_VALUE() execution.\"\"\"\n        call = WindowFunctionCall(\n            function_type=WindowFunctionType.FIRST_VALUE,\n            args=['salary'],\n            window_frame=WindowFrame(partition_by=['dept'], order_by=[('hire_date', 'ASC')]),\n            alias='first_salary'\n        )\n        \n        result = self.executor.execute(self.sample_data.copy(), [call])\n        \n        # Check FIRST_VALUE - should be same for all rows in partition\n        sales_rows = [r for r in result if r['dept'] == <!-- {"role": "tool", "content": "\"\"\"\nQuery Optimizer with Execution Planning and Plan Caching for KosDB v3.2.0\n\nProvides query analysis, cost estimation, execution plan projection\n    JOIN = auto()           # Join operation\nclass OperatorType(Enum):\n    \"\"\"Types of query operators.\"\"\"\n    SCAN = auto()           # Full table scan\n    INDEX_SCAN = auto()     # Index scan\n    SELECT = auto()         # Filter/selection\n    PROJECT = auto()        # Column projection\n    JOIN = auto()           # Join operation\n    SEMI_JOIN = auto()      # Semi-join (for IN/EXISTS subqueries)\n    ANTI_JOIN = auto()      # Anti-join (for NOT IN/NOT EXISTS)\n    AGGREGATE = auto()      # Aggregation (COUNT, SUM, etc.)\n    SORT = auto()           # Order by\n    LIMIT = auto()          # Limit results\n    INSERT = auto()         # Insert operation\n    UPDATE = auto()         # Update operation\n    DELETE = auto()         # Delete operation\n    access_count: int = 0\n    \n    def touch(self):\n        \"\"\"Update access time and count.\"\"\"\n        self.last_accessed = time.time()\n        self.access_count += 1\n\n\nclass PlanCache:\n    \"\"\"\n    LRU Cache for execution plans with configurable size and statistics.\n    \"\"\"\n    \n    def __init__(self, max_size: int = 100):\n        self.max_size = max_size\n        self.cache: OrderedDict[str, PlanCacheEntry] = OrderedDict()\n        self.stats = {\n            'hits': 0,\n            'misses': 0,\n            'evictions': 0,\n            'invalidations': 0\n        }\n        self.dependent_tables: Dict[str, Set[str]] = {}  # cache_key -> tables\n    \n    def get(self, key: str) -> Optional['ExecutionPlan']:\n        \"\"\"Get plan from cache (updates LRU).\"\"\"\n        if key in self.cache:\n            entry = self.cache.pop(key)  # Remove to re-add at end\n            entry.touch()\n            self.cache[key] = entry  # Re-add (most recent)\n            self.stats['hits'] += 1\n            return entry.plan\n        self.stats['misses'] += 1\n        return None\n    \n    def put(self, key: str, plan: 'ExecutionPlan', tables: Set[str]):\n        \"\"\"Add plan to cache.\"\"\"\n        # Evict if necessary\n        while len(self.cache) >= self.max_size:\n            self._evict_lru()\n        \n        entry = PlanCacheEntry(\n            plan=plan,\n            created_at=time.time(),\n            last_accessed=time.time(),\n            access_count=1\n        )\n        self.cache[key] = entry\n        self.dependent_tables[key] = tables\n    \n    def _evict_lru(self):\n        \"\"\"Evict least recently used entry.\"\"\"\n        if self.cache:\n            oldest_key = next(iter(self.cache))\n            del self.cache[oldest_key]\n            del self.dependent_tables[oldest_key]\n            self.stats['evictions'] += 1\n    \n    def invalidate(self, table_name: Optional[str] = None):\n        \"\"\"\n        Invalidate cache entries.\n        \n        Args:\n            table_name: If provided, invalidate only entries depending on this table.\n                       If None, invalidate all entries.\n        \"\"\"\n        if table_name is None:\n            # Clear all\n            count = len(self.cache)\n            self.cache.clear()\n            self.dependent_tables.clear()\n            self.stats['invalidations'] += count\n        else:\n            # Invalidate entries depending on table\n            keys_to_remove = [\n                key for key, tables in self.dependent_tables.items()\n                if table_name in tables\n            ]\n            for key in keys_to_remove:\n                del self.cache[key]\n                del self.dependent_tables[key]\n                self.stats['invalidations'] += 1\n    \n    def get_stats(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Get cache statistics.\"\"\"\n        total_requests = self.stats['hits'] + self.stats['misses']\n        hit_rate = self.stats['hits'] / total_requests if total_requests > 0 else 0.0\n        \n        return {\n            'size': len(self.cache),\n            'max_size': self.max_size,\n            'hits': self.stats['hits'],\n            'misses': self.stats['misses'],\n            'evictions': self.stats['evictions'],\n            'invalidations': self.stats['invalidations'],\n            'hit_rate': round(hit_rate, 4),\n            'miss_rate': round(1 - hit_rate, 4)\n        }\n    \n    def explain(self) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Generate human-readable cache status.\"\"\"\n        stats = self.get_stats()\n        \n        lines = [\n            \"Plan Cache Status:\",\n            \"=\" * 50,\n            f\"Size: {stats['size']} / {stats['max_size']} entries\",\n            f\"Hit Rate: {stats['hit_rate']*100:.2f}%\",\n            f\"Miss Rate: {stats['miss_rate']*100:.2f}%\",\n            f\"Total Hits: {stats['hits']}\",\n            f\"Total Misses: {stats['misses']}\",\n            f\"Evictions: {stats['evictions']}\",\n            f\"Invalidations: {stats['invalidations']}\",\n            \"\",\n            \"Cached Plans:\",\n            \"-\" * 30\n        ]\n        \n        for key, entry in self.cache.items():\n            age = time.time() - entry.created_at\n            last_used = time.time() - entry.last_accessed\n            lines.append(f\"  {key[:16]}... : {entry.access_count} accesses, \"\n                        f\"age={age:.0f}s, last_used={last_used:.0f}s ago\")\n        \n        return \"\\n\".join(lines)\n    \n    def get_column_selectivity(self, column: str) -> float:\n        \"\"\"Get selectivity (0-1) of column.\"\"\"\n        distinct = self.get_column_cardinality(column)\n        if distinct == 0:\n            return 1.0\n        return min(1.0, 1.0 / distinct)\n    \n    def has_index(self, column: str) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"Check if column has index.\"\"\"\n        return column in self.index_stats\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass Operator:\n    \"\"\"Represents an operation in execution plan.\"\"\"\n    op_type: OperatorType\n    table: Optional[str] = None\n    columns: Optional[List[str]] = None\n    condition: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None\n    estimated_rows: int = 0\n    estimated_cost: float = 0.0\n    children: List['Operator'] = field(default_factory=list)\n    \n    # Join specific\n    join_type: Optional[JoinType] = None\n    join_condition: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None\n    left_table: Optional[str] = None\n    right_table: Optional[str] = None\n    \n    # Index specific\n    index_name: Optional[str] = None\n    \n    def to_dict(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Convert to dictionary representation.\"\"\"\n        result = {\n            'type': self.op_type.name,\n            'estimated_rows': self.estimated_rows,\n            'estimated_cost': round(self.estimated_cost, 4),\n        }\n        \n        if self.table:\n            result['table'] = self.table\n        if self.columns:\n            result['columns'] = self.columns\n        if self.condition:\n            result['condition'] = self.condition\n        if self.join_type:\n            result['join_type'] = self.join_type.name\n        if self.index_name:\n            result['index'] = self.index_name\n        \n        if self.children:\n            result['children'] = [c.to_dict() for c in self.children]\n        \n        return result\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass ExecutionPlan:\n    \"\"\"Complete execution plan for a query.\"\"\"\n    root: Operator\n    total_cost: float\n    estimated_rows: int\n    statistics: Dict[str, Any] = field(default_factory=dict)\n    \n    def to_dict(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Convert to dictionary.\"\"\"\n        return {\n            'plan': self.root.to_dict(),\n            'total_cost': round(self.total_cost, 4),\n            'estimated_rows': self.estimated_rows,\n            'statistics': self.statistics\n        }\n    \n    def explain(self) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Generate human-readable explanation.\"\"\"\n        lines = [\"Execution Plan:\", \"=\" * 50]\n        self._explain_operator(self.root, 0, lines)\n        lines.append(f\"\\nTotal Cost: {self.total_cost:.4f}\")\n        lines.append(f\"Estimated Rows: {self.estimated_rows}\")\n        return \"\\n\".join(lines)\n    \n    def _explain_operator(self, op: Operator, depth: int, lines: List[str]):\n        \"\"\"Recursively explain operators.\"\"\"\n        indent = \"  \" * depth\n        cost_info = f\" (cost={op.estimated_cost:.2f}, rows={op.estimated_rows})\"\n        \n        if op.op_type == OperatorType.SCAN:\n            lines.append(f\"{indent}\u2192 Seq Scan on {op.table}{cost_info}\")\n        elif op.op_type == OperatorType.INDEX_SCAN:\n            lines.append(f\"{indent}\u2192 Index Scan using {op.index_name} on {op.table}{cost_info}\")\n        elif op.op_type == OperatorType.SELECT:\n            lines.append(f\"{indent}\u2192 Filter: {op.condition}{cost_info}\")\n        elif op.op_type == OperatorType.PROJECT:\n            cols = \", \".join(op.columns) if op.columns else \"*\"\n            lines.append(f\"{indent}\u2192 Project: {cols}{cost_info}\")\n        elif op.op_type == OperatorType.JOIN:\n            join = f\"{op.join_type.name} Join\" if op.join_type else \"Join\"\n            lines.append(f\"{indent}\u2192 {join}{cost_info}\")\n        elif op.op_type == OperatorType.SORT:\n            lines.append(f\"{indent}\u2192 Sort{cost_info}\")\n        elif op.op_type == OperatorType.LIMIT:\n            lines.append(f\"{indent}\u2192 Limit{cost_info}\")\n        elif op.op_type == OperatorType.AGGREGATE:\n            lines.append(f\"{indent}\u2192 Aggregate{cost_info}\")\n        \n        for child in op.children:\n            self._explain_operator(child, depth + 1, lines)\n\n\nclass CostModel:\n    \"\"\"\n    Cost model for query operations.\n    Assigns costs based on I/O and CPU estimates.\n    \"\"\"\n    \n    # Base costs\n    SEQ_PAGE_COST = 1.0           # Cost to read one page sequentially\n    RANDOM_PAGE_COST = 4.0        # Cost to read one page randomly (index)\n    CPU_TUPLE_COST = 0.01         # Cost to process one tuple\n    CPU_INDEX_TUPLE_COST = 0.005  # Cost to process index tuple\n    CPU_OPERATOR_COST = 0.0025    # Cost to execute one operator\n    \n    def __init__(self):\n        self.statistics: Dict[str, Statistics] = {}\n    \n    def add_statistics(self, table: str, stats: Statistics):\n        \"\"\"Add statistics for a table.\"\"\"\n        self.statistics[table] = stats\n    \n    def estimate_scan_cost(self, table: str, \n                          use_index: bool = False,\n                          index_column: Optional[str] = None) -> Tuple[float, int]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Estimate cost of table scan.\n        \n        Returns: (cost, estimated_rows)\n        \"\"\"\n        stats = self.statistics.get(table)\n        if not stats:\n            return (self.SEQ_PAGE_COST * 10, 1000)  # Default estimate\n        \n        rows = stats.row_count\n        \n        if use_index and index_column and stats.has_index(index_column):\n            # Index scan - fewer pages, more random access\n            selectivity = stats.get_column_selectivity(index_column)\n            estimated_rows = max(1, int(rows * selectivity))\n            \n            # Cost: random page reads + index processing\n            index_pages = max(1, estimated_rows / 100)  # Assume 100 rows per page\n            cost = (index_pages * self.RANDOM_PAGE_COST + \n                   estimated_rows * self.CPU_INDEX_TUPLE_COST +\n                   estimated_rows * self.CPU_TUPLE_COST)\n        else:\n            # Sequential scan\n            pages = max(1, rows / 100)  # Assume 100 rows per page\n            cost = pages * self.SEQ_PAGE_COST + rows * self.CPU_TUPLE_COST\n            estimated_rows = rows\n        \n        return (cost, estimated_rows)\n    \n    def estimate_filter_cost(self, input_rows: int, \n                            condition: Dict[str, Any]) -> Tuple[float, int]:\n        \"\"\"Estimate cost of filter operation.\"\"\"\n        # Simple selectivity estimate\n        selectivity = 0.1  # Default: 10% pass through\n        \n        if 'column' in condition and 'op' in condition:\n            col = condition['column']\n            op = condition['op']\n            \n            if op == '=':\n                selectivity = 0.01  # Equality is very selective\n            elif op in ('>', '<', '>=', '<='):\n                selectivity = 0.3   # Range is moderately selective\n            elif op == 'LIKE':\n                selectivity = 0.2   # Pattern match\n        \n        estimated_rows = max(1, int(input_rows * selectivity))\n        cost = input_rows * self.CPU_OPERATOR_COST\n        \n        return (cost, estimated_rows)\n    \n    def estimate_join_cost(self, left_rows: int, right_rows: int,\n                          join_type: JoinType) -> Tuple[float, int]:\n        \"\"\"Estimate cost of join operation.\"\"\"\n        if join_type == JoinType.NESTED_LOOP:\n            cost = left_rows * right_rows * self.CPU_OPERATOR_COST\n            rows = left_rows * right_rows\n        elif join_type == JoinType.HASH_JOIN:\n            # Build hash table + probe\n            cost = (left_rows + right_rows) * self.CPU_OPERATOR_COST * 2\n            rows = min(left_rows, right_rows)  # Assume some reduction\n        elif join_type == JoinType.MERGE_JOIN:\n            # Sort + merge\n            cost = (left_rows * 0.1 + right_rows * 0.1 + \n                   (left_rows + right_rows) * self.CPU_OPERATOR_COST)\n            rows = min(left_rows, right_rows)\n        else:\n            cost = left_rows * right_rows * self.CPU_OPERATOR_COST\n            rows = left_rows * right_rows\n        \n        return (cost, max(1, rows))\n    \n    def estimate_sort_cost(self, input_rows: int) -> Tuple[float, int]:\n        \"\"\"Estimate cost of sort operation.\"\"\"\n        # O(n log n) complexity\n        import math\n        cost = input_rows * math.log2(max(2, input_rows)) * self.CPU_OPERATOR_COST\n        return (cost, input_rows)\n    \n    def estimate_aggregate_cost(self, input_rows: int, \n                                 group_by: Optional[List[str]] = None) -> Tuple[float, int]:\n        \"\"\"Estimate cost of aggregation.\"\"\"\n        cost = input_rows * self.CPU_OPERATOR_COST\n        \n        if group_by:\n            # Assume reduction by grouping\n            output_rows = max(1, input_rows // 10)\n        else:\n            # Scalar aggregate - single result\n            output_rows = 1\n        \n        return (cost, output_rows)\n\n\nclass QueryParser:\n    \"\"\"\n    Parses SQL-like queries into structured representation.\n    \"\"\"\n    \n    def __init__(self):\n        self.parsed: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None\n    \n    def parse(self, query: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse query string into structured form.\"\"\"\n        query = query.strip()\n        upper = query.upper()\n        \n        if upper.startswith('SELECT'):\n            return self._parse_select(query)\n        elif upper.startswith('INSERT'):\n            return self._parse_insert(query)\n        elif upper.startswith('UPDATE'):\n            return self._parse_update(query)\n        elif upper.startswith('DELETE'):\n            return self._parse_delete(query)\n        else:\n            raise ValueError(f\"Unsupported query type: {query[:50]}...\")\n    \n    def _parse_select(self, query: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse SELECT statement.\"\"\"\n        result = {\n            'type': 'SELECT',\n            'columns': [],\n            'table': None,\n            'where': None,\n            'order_by': None,\n            'order_desc': False,\n            'limit': None\n        }\n        \n        # Extract columns\n        match = re.search(r'SELECT\\s+(.+?)\\s+FROM', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            cols_str = match.group(1).strip()\n            if cols_str == '*':\n                result['columns'] = ['*']\n            else:\n                result['columns'] = [c.strip() for c in cols_str.split(',')]\n        \n        # Extract table\n        match = re.search(r'FROM\\s+(\\w+)', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['table'] = match.group(1)\n        \n        # Extract WHERE\n        match = re.search(r'WHERE\\s+(.+?)(?:ORDER BY|LIMIT|$)', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['where'] = self._parse_where(match.group(1).strip())\n        \n        # Extract ORDER BY\n        match = re.search(r'ORDER BY\\s+(\\w+)\\s*(ASC|DESC)?', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['order_by'] = match.group(1)\n            result['order_desc'] = match.group(2) and match.group(2).upper() == 'DESC'\n        \n        # Extract LIMIT\n        match = re.search(r'LIMIT\\s+(\\d+)', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['limit'] = int(match.group(1))\n        \n        return result\n    \n    def _parse_insert(self, query: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse INSERT statement.\"\"\"\n        result = {'type': 'INSERT', 'table': None, 'values': []}\n        \n        match = re.search(r'INTO\\s+(\\w+)', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['table'] = match.group(1)\n        \n        match = re.search(r'VALUES\\s*\\(([^)]+)\\)', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            values_str = match.group(1)\n            result['values'] = self._parse_values(values_str)\n        \n        return result\n    \n    def _parse_update(self, query: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse UPDATE statement.\"\"\"\n        result = {'type': 'UPDATE', 'table': None, 'set': {}, 'where': None}\n        \n        match = re.search(r'UPDATE\\s+(\\w+)', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['table'] = match.group(1)\n        \n        match = re.search(r'SET\\s+(.+?)(?:WHERE|$)', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['set'] = self._parse_set_clause(match.group(1).strip())\n        \n        match = re.search(r'WHERE\\s+(.+)$', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['where'] = self._parse_where(match.group(1).strip())\n        \n        return result\n    \n    def _parse_delete(self, query: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse DELETE statement.\"\"\"\n        result = {'type': 'DELETE', 'table': None, 'where': None}\n        \n        match = re.search(r'FROM\\s+(\\w+)', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['table'] = match.group(1)\n        \n        match = re.search(r'WHERE\\s+(.+)$', query, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            result['where'] = self._parse_where(match.group(1).strip())\n        \n        return result\n    \n    def _parse_where(self, where_str: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse WHERE clause.\"\"\"\n        # Simple condition parsing\n        where_str = where_str.strip()\n        \n        # Try equality\n        match = re.match(r'(\\w+)\\s*=\\s*(.+)', where_str)\n        if match:\n            return {\n                'column': match.group(1),\n                'op': '=',\n                'value': self._parse_value(match.group(2))\n            }\n        \n        # Try comparison operators\n        match = re.match(r'(\\w+)\\s*(>=?|<=?)\\s*(.+)', where_str)\n        if match:\n            return {\n                'column': match.group(1),\n                'op': match.group(2),\n                'value': self._parse_value(match.group(3))\n            }\n        \n        # Try LIKE\n        match = re.match(r'(\\w+)\\s+LIKE\\s+(.+)', where_str, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if match:\n            return {\n                'column': match.group(1),\n                'op': 'LIKE',\n                'value': self._parse_value(match.group(2))\n            }\n        \n        return {'raw': where_str}\n    \n    def _parse_values(self, values_str: str) -> List[Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse VALUES clause.\"\"\"\n        values = []\n        for val in values_str.split(','):\n            val = val.strip()\n            values.append(self._parse_value(val))\n        return values\n    \n    def and return execution plan.\n        \n        Args:\n            query: SQL query string\n            use_cache: Whether to use plan cache\n        \n        Returns:\n            ExecutionPlan with optimal operations\n        \"\"\"\n        # Check cache\n        cache_key = self._get_cache_key(query)\n        if use_cache:\n            cached_plan = self.plan_cache.get(cache_key)\n   tables = self._extract_tables(parsed)\n        \n        # Generate plan based on query type\n        if parsed['type'] == 'SELECT':\n            plan = self._optimize_select(parsed)\n        elif parsed['type'] == 'INSERT':\n            plan = self._optimize_insert(parsed)\n        elif parsed['type'] == 'UPDATE':\n            plan = self._optimize_update(parsed)\n        elif parsed['type'] use_cache:\n            self.plan_cache.put(cache_key, plan, tables)\n        \n        return plan\n    \n    def _get_cache_key(self, query: str) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Generate cache key for query.\"\"\"\n        # Normalize query for caching\n        normalized = ' '.join(query.split()).lower()\n        return hashlib.md5(normalized.encode()).hexdigest()\n    \n    def _extract_tables(self, parsed: Dict[str, Any]) -> Set[str]:\n        \"\"\"Extract table names from parsed query for cache dependencies.\"\"\"\n        tables = set()\n        \n        if 'table' in  def _optimize_select(self, parsed: Dict[str, Any]) -> ExecutionPlan:\n        \"\"\"Generate execution plan for SELECT.\"\"\"\n        table = parsed['table']\n        where = parsed.get('where')\n > <contentOfFile>"""
> CTE Engine for KosDB v3.3.0
> 
> Provides Common Table Expression (CTE) support:
> - Non-recursive CTEs
> - Recursive CTEs (WITH RECURSIVE)
> - Multiple CTEs in single query
> - Proper scoping and reference resolution
> """
> 
> from typing import Dict, Any, List, Optional, Set, Tuple
> from dataclasses import dataclass, field
> from enum import ...

<!-- {"role": "assistant", "content": "I'll implement CTEs (Common Table Expressions) for KosDB v3.3.0. Let me start by creating the CTE module.  <CreateFile>\n<fileName>cte_engine.py</fileName>\n<contentOfFile>\"\"\"\nCTE Engine for KosDB v3.3.0\n\nProvides Common Table Expression (CTE) support:\n- Non-recursive CTEs\n- Recursive CTEs (WITH RECURSIVE)\n- Multiple CTEs in single query\n- Proper scoping and reference resolution\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom typing import Dict, Any, List, Optional, Set, Tuple\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass, field\nfrom enum import Enum\n\n\nclass CTENodeType(Enum):\n    \"\"\"Types of CTE nodes.\"\"\"\n    NON_RECURSIVE = \"NON_RECURSIVE\"\n    RECURSIVE_ANCHOR = \"RECURSIVE_ANCHOR\"\n    RECURSIVE_ITERATIVE = \"RECURSIVE_ITERATIVE\"\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass CTE:\n    \"\"\"Represents a single Common Table Expression.\"\"\"\n    name: str\n    columns: Optional[List[str]]  # Explicit column names (optional)\n    query: Dict[str, Any]  # Parsed query\n    node_type: CTENodeType\n    is_recursive: bool = False\n    \n    # For recursive CTEs\n    anchor_query: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None\n    recursive_query: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None\n    \n    # Execution results (transient)\n    result_data: List[Dict[str, Any]] = field(default_factory=list)\n    is_executed: bool = False\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass CTEDefinition:\n    \"\"\"Complete CTE definition from WITH clause.\"\"\"\n    ctes: List[CTE]\n    is_recursive: bool = False\n    main_query: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None\n\n\nclass CTEEngine:\n    \"\"\"\n    Engine for executing Common Table Expressions.\n    \n    Handles:\n    - CTE registration and scoping\n    - Non-recursive CTE execution\n    - Recursive CTE execution (fixed-point iteration)\n    - Reference resolution\n    \"\"\"\n    \n    def __init__(self, execute_query_func=None):\n        self.ctes: Dict[str, CTE] = {}\n        self.execute_query = execute_query_func or self._default_execute\n        self.max_recursive_iterations = 100  # Prevent infinite recursion\n    \n    def register_ctes(self, cte_def: CTEDefinition):\n        \"\"\"Register CTEs from definition.\"\"\"\n        self.ctes.clear()\n        for cte in cte_def.ctes:\n            self.ctes[cte.name.upper()] = cte\n    \n    def execute_cte(self, cte_name: str) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Execute a CTE and return results.\n        \n        Args:\n            cte_name: Name of the CTE to execute\n        \n        Returns:\n            List of result rows\n        \"\"\"\n        cte_name = cte_name.upper()\n        cte = self.ctes.get(cte_name)\n        \n        if not cte:\n            raise ValueError(f\"CTE not found: {cte_name}\")\n        \n        if cte.is_executed:\n            return cte.result_data\n        \n        if cte.is_recursive:\n            result = self._execute_recursive_cte(cte)\n        else:\n            result = self._execute_non_recursive_cte(cte)\n        \n        cte.result_data = result\n        cte.is_executed = True\n        \n        return result\n    \n    def _execute_non_recursive_cte(self, cte: CTE) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:\n        \"\"\"Execute a non-recursive CTE.\"\"\"\n        # Execute the CTE query\n        return self.execute_query(cte.query)\n    \n    def _execute_recursive_cte(self, cte: CTE) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Execute a recursive CTE using fixed-point iteration.\n        \n        Algorithm:\n        1. Execute anchor query (base case)\n        2. Execute recursive query with current results\n        3. Union results\n        4. Repeat until no new rows or max iterations reached\n        \"\"\"\n        if not cte.anchor_query or not cte.recursive_query:\n            raise ValueError(f\"Recursive CTE {cte.name} missing anchor or recursive query\")\n        \n        # Execute anchor query\n        result = self.execute_query(cte.anchor_query)\n        all_results = result.copy()\n        \n        # Iterative execution\n        for iteration in range(self.max_recursive_iterations):\n            # Execute recursive query with current results as input\n            new_rows = self._execute_recursive_step(\n                cte.recursive_query, \n                cte.name,\n                result\n            )\n            \n            if not new_rows:\n                break  # Fixed point reached\n            \n            # Add new rows (UNION semantics - remove duplicates)\n            existing_keys = {self._row_key(r) for r in all_results}\n            for row in new_rows:\n                key = self._row_key(row)\n                if key not in existing_keys:\n                    all_results.append(row)\n                    existing_keys.add(key)\n            \n            result = new_rows  # Continue with new rows only\n        \n        return all_results\n    \n    def _execute_recursive_step(self, query: Dict[str, Any], \n                                cte_name: str, \n                                current_data: List[Dict[str, Any]]) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:\n        \"\"\"Execute one step of recursive CTE.\"\"\"\n        # Temporarily register current data as CTE result\n        if cte_name.upper() in self.ctes:\n            self.ctes[cte_name.upper()].result_data = current_data\n        \n        return self.execute_query(query)\n    \n    def _row_key(self, row: Dict[str, Any]) -> Tuple:\n        \"\"\"Generate hashable key for row (for duplicate detection).\"\"\"\n        return tuple(sorted(row.items()))\n    \n    def _default_execute(self, query: Dict[str, Any]) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:\n        \"\"\"Default query execution (placeholder).\"\"\"\n        # This should be replaced with actual database execution\n        return []\n    \n    def resolve_cte_reference(self, table_name: str) -> Optional[CTE]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Check if table name refers to a CTE.\n        \n        Args:\n            table_name: Table name to check\n        \n        Returns:\n            CTE if found, None otherwise\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.ctes.get(table_name.upper())\n    \n    def get_cte_columns(self, cte_name: str) -> List[str]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Get column names for a CTE.\n        \n        Args:\n            cte_name: Name of the CTE\n        \n        Returns:\n            List of column names\n        \"\"\"\n        cte_name = cte_name.upper()\n        cte = self.ctes.get(cte_name)\n        \n        if not cte:\n            return []\n        \n        if cte.columns:\n            return cte.columns\n        \n        # Infer from result data\n        if cte.result_data:\n            return list(cte.result_data[0].keys())\n        \n        return []\n    \n    def clear(self):\n        \"\"\"Clear all CTEs.\"\"\"\n        self.ctes.clear()\n    \n    def get_execution_order(self) -> List[str]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Get topological order for CTE execution.\n        \n        Handles dependencies between CTEs.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Build dependency graph\n        dependencies: Dict[str, Set[str]] = {}\n        \n        for name, cte in self.ctes.items():\n            deps = self._extract_dependencies(cte.query)\n            dependencies[name] = deps\n        \n        # Topological sort\n        visited: Set[str] = set()\n        order: List[str] = []\n        \n        def visit(n: str):\n            if n in visited:\n                return\n            visited.add(n)\n            for dep in dependencies.get(n, []):\n                if dep in self.ctes:  # Only visit CTE dependencies\n                    visit(dep)\n            order.append(n)\n        \n        for name in self.ctes:\n            visit(name)\n        \n        return order\n    \n    def _extract_dependencies(self, query: Dict[str, Any]) -> Set[str]:\n        \"\"\"Extract CTE dependencies from query.\"\"\"\n        deps = set()\n        \n        # Check FROM clause\n        table = query.get('table')\n        if table and isinstance(table, str):\n            deps.add(table.upper())\n        \n        # Check subqueries\n        # This is simplified - full implementation would parse all subqueries\n        \n        return deps\n\n\ndef parse_cte_definition(sql: str) -> Optional[CTEDefinition]:\n    \"\"\"\n    Parse WITH clause from SQL.\n    \n    Args:\n        sql: SQL query with CTE\n    \n    Returns:\n        CTEDefinition or None if no CTE\n    \"\"\"\n    import re\n    \n    # Match WITH [RECURSIVE] clause\n    pattern = r'^\\s*WITH\\s+(RECURSIVE\\s+)?(.+?)\\s+SELECT\\s+'\n    match = re.match(pattern, sql, re.IGNORECASE | re.DOTALL)\n    \n    if not match:\n        return None\n    \n    is_recursive = bool(match.group(1))\n    cte_part = match.group(2)\n    \n    # Split CTEs (handle parentheses carefully)\n    ctes = []\n    current_cte = \"\"\n    paren_depth = 0\n    \n    for char in cte_part:\n        if char == '(':\n            paren_depth += 1\n            current_cte += char\n        elif char == ')':\n            paren_depth -= 1\n            current_cte += char\n        elif char == ',' and paren_depth == 0:\n            # End of CTE\n            cte = _parse_single_cte(current_cte.strip(), is_recursive)\n            if cte:\n                ctes.append(cte)\n            current_cte = \"\"\n        else:\n            current_cte += char\n    \n    # Last CTE\n    if current_cte.strip():\n        cte = _parse_single_cte(current_cte.strip(), is_recursive)\n        if cte:\n            ctes.append(cte)\n    \n    return CTEDefinition(\n        ctes=ctes,\n        is_recursive=is_recursive\n    )\n\n\ndef _parse_single_cte(cte_str: str, is_recursive: bool) -> Optional[CTE]:\n    \"\"\"Parse a single CTE definition.\"\"\"\n    import re\n    \n    # Pattern: name [(cols)] AS (query)\n    pattern = r'(\\w+)\\s*(?:\\(([^)]+)\\))?\\s+AS\\s*\\((.+)\\)'\n    match = re.match(pattern, cte_str.strip(), re.IGNORECASE | re.DOTALL)\n    \n    if not match:\n        return None\n    \n    name = match.group(1)\n    columns = None\n    if match.group(2):\n        columns = [c.strip() for c in match.group(2).split(',')]\n    \n    query_str = match.group(3).strip()\n    \n    # Check for recursive UNION/UNION ALL\n    union_pattern = r'(.+?)\\s+UNION\\s+(?:ALL\\s+)?(.+)'\n    union_match = re.match(union_pattern, query_str, re.IGNORECASE | re.DOTALL)\n    \n    if is_recursive and union_match:\n        # Recursive CTE with anchor and recursive parts\n        return CTE(\n            name=name,\n            columns=columns,\n            query={'raw': query_str},\n            node_type=CTENodeType.RECURSIVE_ANCHOR,\n            is_recursive=True,\n            anchor_query={'raw': union_match.group(1).strip()},\n            recursive_query={'raw': union_match.group(2).strip()}\n        )\n    \n    # Non-recursive CTE\n    return CTE(\n        name=name,\n        columns=columns,\n        query={'raw': query_str},\n        node_type=CTENodeType.NON_RECURSIVE,\n        is_recursive=False\n    )\n\n\n# Example usage\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    # Example 1: Simple non-recursive CTE\n    sql1 = \"\"\"\n        WITH sales_summary AS (\n            SELECT dept, SUM(sales) as total_sales\n            FROM sales\n            GROUP BY dept\n        )\n        SELECT * FROM sales_summary WHERE total_sales > 10000\n    \"\"\"\n    \n    cte_def = parse_cte_definition(sql1)\n    if cte_def:\n        print(f\"Found {len(cte_def.ctes)} CTE(s)\")\n        for cte in cte_def.ctes:\n            print(f\"  CTE: {cte.name}, Recursive: {cte.is_recursive}\")\n    \n    # Check for window functions: FUNC(args) OVER (...)\n            window_match = re.match(r'(\\w+)\\s*\\(([^)]*)\\)\\s+OVER\\s*\\(([^)]+)\\)(?:\\s+AS\\s+(\\w+))?', part, re.IGNORECASE)\n            if window_match:\n                func_name = window_match.group(1).upper()\n                args = window_match.group(2).strip()\n                over_clause = window_match.group(3).strip()\n                alias = window_match.group(4)\n                \n                columns.append({\n                    'type': 'WINDOW_FUNCTION',\n                    'function': func_name,\n                    'args': [a.strip() for a in args.split(',')] if args else [],\n                    'over': self._parse_over_clause(over_clause),\n                    'alias': alias or f\"{func_name.lower()}_result\"\n                })\n                continue\n            \n            # Check for JSON extraction: column->path or column->>path\n            json_match = re.match(r'(\\w+)(->>?)(.+)', part)\n            if json_match:\n                col_name = json_match.group(1)\n                operator = json_match.group(2)\n                json_path = json_match.group(3).strip()\n                columns.append({\n                    'name': col_name,\n                    'json_path': json_path,\n                    'json_as_text': operator == '->>'\n                })\n            elif ' AS ' in part.upper():\n                parts = part.split()\n                col_name = parts[0]\n                alias = parts[-1]\n                columns.append({'name': col_name, 'alias': alias})\n            else:\n                columns.append(part)\n        \n        return columns\n    \n    def _parse_over_clause(self, over_str: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse OVER clause for window functions.\"\"\"\n        result = {\n            'partition_by': None,\n            'order_by': None\n        }\n        \n        # Check if any reference is to a different table\n        for table, col in outer_refs:\n            if table != subquery_table:\n                return True\n        \n        return False\n    \n    def _split_where_conditions(self, where_str: str) -> List[str]:\n        \"\"\"Split WHERE clause by AND/OR respecting parentheses.\"\"\"\n        parts = []\n        current = \"\"\n        depth = 0\n        i = 0\n        \n        while i < len(where_str):\n            char = where_str[i]\n            \n            if char == '(':\n                depth += 1\n                current += char\n            elif char == ')':\n                depth -= 1\n                current += char\n            elif depth == 0:\n                # Check for AND/OR\n                remaining = where_str[i:].upper()\n                if remaining.startswith('AND ') or remaining.startswith('AND\\\\t'):\n                    parts.append(current)\n                    current = \"\"\n                    i += 3  # Skip 'AND'\n                    continue\n                elif remaining.startswith('OR ') or remaining.startswith('OR\\\\t'):\n                    parts.append(current)\n                    current = \"\"\n                    i += 2  # AGAINST ... syntax for full-text search.\"\"\"\n        pattern = re.compile(\n            r'^\\s*MATCH\\s*\\((?P<columns>[\\w\\s,]+)\\)\\s+AGAINST\\s*\\(\\s*[\\'\\\"](?P<query>[^\\'\\\"]+)[\\'\\\"]\\s*(?:\\s+IN\\s+(?P<mode>[\\w\\s]+)\\s+MODE)?(?:\\s+(?P<expansion>WITH\\s+QUERY\\s+EXPANSION))?\\s*\\)\\s*$',\n            re.IGNORECASE\n        )\n        \n        match = pattern.match(sql)\n        if match:\n            params = match.groupdict()\n            columns = [c.strip() for c in mode_str:\n                    mode = 'BOOLEAN'\n                elif 'NATURAL' in mode_str:\n                    mode = 'NATURAL'\n            \n            if params.get('expansion'):\n _parse_select_columns(self, columns_str: str) -> List[Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse SELECT column list with JSON extraction support.\"\"\"\n        columns = []\n        parts = depth = 0\n        \n        for char in args_str:\n            if char == '(':\n                depth += 1\n                current += char\n            elif char == ')':\n                depth -= 1\n                current += char\n            elif char == ',' and depth == 0:\n                parts.append(current)\n                current = \"\"\n            else:\n                current += char\n        \n        if current.strip():\n            parts.append(current)\n        \n        return parts\n    \n    def _parse_column_definition(self, col_def: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Parse a single column definition.\"\"\"\n        col_info = {\n            'name': None,\n            'type': 'TEXT',\n            'primary_key': False,\n            'index': False,\n            'unique': False,\n            'foreign_key': None,\n            'check': None,\n            'nullable': True,\n            'default': None\n        }\n        \n        # Check for PRIMARY KEY constraint\n        pk_match = re.match(r'^\\s*PRIMARY\\s+KEY\\s*\\(\\s*(\\w+)\\s*\\)\\s*$', col_def, re.IGNORECASE)\n        if pk_match:\n            return {'constraint_type': 'PRIMARY_KEY', <!-- {"role": "assistant", "content": "Let me add the CTE parsing method to the parser:  <ReplaceLine>\n<fileName>parser.py</fileName>\n<fromLine>176</fromLine>\n<toLine>200</toLine>\n<replacement>        # Match WITH [RECURSIVE] clause\n        cte_pattern = re.compile(\n            r'^\\\\s*WITH\\\\s+(RECURSIVE\\\\s+)?(.+?)\\\\s+SELECT\\\\s+',\n            re.IGNORECASE | re.DOTALL\n        )\n        \n        match = cte_pattern.match(sql)\n        if not match:\n            return None\n        \n        is_recursive = bool(match.group(1))\n        cte_part = match.group(2).strip()\n        \n        # Parse CTE definitions\n        ctes = self._parse_cte_definitions(cte_part, is_recursive)\n        \n        if not ctes:\n            return None\n        \n        # Extract main query (after CTE definitions)\n        main_query_match = re.search(\n            r'SELECT\\\\s+(.+)$',\n            sql,\n            re.IGNORECASE | re.DOTALL\n        )\n        \n        main_query = main_query_match.group(1) if main_query_match else None\n        \n        return 'SELECT_WITH_CTE', {\n            'ctes': ctes,\n            'is_recursive': is_recursive,\n            'main_query': main_query,\n            'raw_sql': sql\n        }\n    \n    def _parse_cte_definitions(self, cte_part: str, is_recursive: bool) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:\n        \"\"\"Parse individual CTE definitions from WITH clause.\"\"\"\n        ctes = []\n        current_cte = \"\"\n        paren_depth = 0\n        \n        for char in cte_part:\n            if char == '(':\n                paren_depth += 1\n                current_cte += char\n            elif char == ')':\n                paren_depth -= 1\n                current_cte += char\n            elif char == ',' and paren_depth == 0:\n                # <!-- {"role": "assistant", "content": "Now let me add the remaining parser methods and fix the file structure:  <ReplaceLine>\n<fileName>parser.py</fileName>\n<fromLine>294</fromLine>\n<toLine>294</toLine>\n<replacement>        return result\n    \n    def _parse_where_clause(self, where_str: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Parse WHERE clause with support for subqueries.\n        \n        Supports:\n        - Simple conditions: col = value\n        - IN/NOT IN subqueries: col IN (SELECT ...)\n        - EXISTS/NOT EXISTS: EXISTS (SELECT ...)\n        - Scalar subqueries: col = (SELECT ...)\n        \"\"\"\n        where_str = where_str.strip()\n        conditions = []\n        \n        # Check if it's a subquery\n                if subquery_str.upper().startswith('SELECT'):\n                    subquery = self._parse_subquery(subquery_str)\n                    conditions.append({\n                        'type': 'IN_SUBQUERY',\n                        'column': col,\n                        'subquery': subquery,\n                        'negated': is_not\n                    })\n                    continue\n                else:\n                    # Check for EXISTS/NOT EXISTS\n            exists_match = re.match(r'(NOT\\\\s+)?EXISTS\\\\s*\\\\((.+)\\\\)\\\\s*$', part, re.IGNORECASE)\n            if exists_match:\n                is_not = exists_match.group(1) is not None\n                subquery_str = exists_match.group(2)\n                subquery = self._parse_subquery(subquery_str)\n                conditions.append({\n                    'type': 'EXISTS',\n                    'subquery': subquery,\n                    'negated': is_not\n                })\n                continue\n            \n            # Remove outer parentheses if present\n        while subquery_str.startswith('(') and subquery_str.endswith(')'):\n            inner = subquery_str[1:-1].strip()\n            # Check if parentheses are balanced\n            depth = 0\n            valid = True\n            for char in inner:\n                if char == '(':\n                    depth += 1\n                elif char == ')':\n                    depth -= 1\n                    if depth < 0:\n                        valid = False\n                        break\n            if valid and depth == 0:\n                subquery_str = inner\n            else:\n                break\n        \n        # Let me start by creating the prepared statement cache module:  <CreateFile>\n<fileName>prepared_statement_cache.py</fileName>\n<contentOfFile>\"\"\"\nPrepared Statement Cache for KosDB v3.3.0\n\nProvides secure prepared statement execution with:\n- PREPARE: Create prepared statements with parameter placeholders\n- EXECUTE: Execute prepared statements with bound parameters\n- DEALLOCATE: Remove prepared statements\n\nFeatures:\n- Parameter binding (positional ? and named :param)\n- SQL injection prevention through proper escaping\n- Statement caching with LRU eviction\n- Type inference and validation\n\"\"\"\n\nimport re\nimport hashlib\nimport threading\nfrom typing import Dict, Any, List, Optional, Union, Tuple\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass, field\nfrom enum import Enum, auto\nfrom collections import OrderedDict\nimport time\n\n\nclass ParameterStyle(Enum):\n    \"\"\"Styles of parameter placeholders.\"\"\"\n    QMARK = auto()      # ? (positional)\n    NAMED = auto()      # :name (named)\n    PYFORMAT = auto()   # %(name)s (Python style)\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass PreparedStatement:\n    \"\"\"Represents a prepared statement.\"\"\"\n    name: str\n    sql_template: str\n    parameter_style: ParameterStyle\n    parameters: List[str]  # Parameter names or positions\n    created_at: float = field(default_factory=time.time)\n    last_used: float = field(default_factory=time.time)\n    use_count: int = 0\n    parsed_query: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None\n    \n    def touch(self):\n        \"\"\"Update last used timestamp.\"\"\"\n        self.last_used = time.time()\n        self.use_count += 1\n\n\nclass ParameterBinder:\n    \"\"\"\n    Handles parameter binding for prepared statements.\n    \n    Provides secure parameter substitution to prevent SQL injection.\n    \"\"\"\n    \n    # Type conversion handlers\n    TYPE_HANDLERS = {\n        int: lambda x: str(int(x)),\n        float: lambda x: str(float(x)),\n        bool: lambda x: 'TRUE' if x else 'FALSE',\n        type(None): lambda x: 'NULL',\n    }\n    \n    def __init__(self):\n        self._string_cache: Dict[str, str] = {}\n    \n    def bind_parameters(self, sql_template: str, \n                       parameters: Union[List[Any], Dict[str, Any]],\n                       style: ParameterStyle) -> str:\n        \"\"\"\n        Bind parameters to SQL template securely.\n        \n        Args:\n            sql_template: SQL with placeholders\n            parameters: Values to bind\n            style: Parameter placeholder style\n        \n        Returns:\n            SQL with parameters bound\n        \n        Raises:\n            ValueError: If parameter count mismatch or invalid values\n        \"\"\"\n        if style == ParameterStyle.QMARK:\n            return self._bind_positional(sql_template, parameters)\n        elif style == ParameterStyle.NAMED:\n            return self._bind_named(sql_template, parameters)\n        elif style == ParameterStyle.PYFORMAT:\n            return self._bind_pyformat(sql_template, parameters)\n        else:\n            raise ValueError(f\"Unknown parameter style: {style}\")\n    \n    def _bind_positional(self, sql_template: str, \n                         parameters: List[Any]) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Bind positional ? parameters.\"\"\"\n        parts = sql_template.split('?')\n        \n        if len(parts) - 1 != len(parameters):\n            raise ValueError(\n                f\"Parameter count mismatch: expected {len(parts) - 1}, \"\n                f\"got {len(parameters)}\"\n            )\n        \n        result = []\n        for i, part in enumerate(parts[:-1]):\n            result.append(part)\n            result.append(self._format_value(parameters[i]))\n        result.append(parts[-1])\n        \n        return ''.join(result)\n    \n    def _bind_named(self, sql_template: str, \n                    parameters: Dict[str, Any]) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Bind named :param parameters.\"\"\"\n        def replace_param(match):\n            param_name = match.group(1)\n            if param_name not in parameters:\n                raise ValueError(f\"Missing parameter: {param_name}\")\n            return self._format_value(parameters[param_name])\n        \n        # Pattern matches :param_name (alphanumeric and underscore)\n        return re.sub(r':([a-zA-Z_][a-zA-Z0-9_]*)', replace_param, sql_template)\n    \n    def _bind_pyformat(self, sql_template: str, \n                       parameters: Dict[str, Any]) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Bind Python-style %(name)s parameters.\"\"\"\n        def replace_param(match):\n            param_name = match.group(1)\n            if param_name not in parameters:\n                raise ValueError(f\"Missing parameter: {param_name}\")\n            return self._format_value(parameters[param_name])\n        \n        return re.sub(r'%\\\\(([a-zA-Z_][a-zA-Z0-9_]*)\\\\)s', replace_param, sql_template)\n    \n    def _format_value(self, value: Any) -> str:\n        \"\"\"\n        Format a value for SQL insertion.\n        \n        This is the critical security function - properly escapes\n        all values to prevent SQL injection.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Handle known types\n        handler = self.TYPE_HANDLERS.get(type(value))\n        if handler:\n            return handler(value)\n        \n        # Handle strings - CRITICAL for SQL injection prevention\n        if isinstance(value, str):\n            return self._escape_string(value)\n        \n        # Default: convert to string and escape\n        return self._escape_string(str(value))\n    \n    def _escape_string(self, value: str) -> str:\n        \"\"\"\n        Escape a string value for safe SQL insertion.\n        \n        Implements standard SQL escaping:\n        - Single quotes are doubled (' becomes '')\n        - Backslashes are doubled\n        - Null bytes are removed\n        \"\"\"\n        # Security: Remove null bytes\n        value = value.replace('\\\\x00', '')\n        \n        # Escape backslashes first (before quotes)\n        value = value.replace('\\\\\\\\', '\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\')\n        \n        # Escape single quotes by doubling\n        value = value.replace(\"'\", \"''\")\n        \n        # Wrap in single quotes\n        return f\"'{value}'\"\n    \n    def validate_parameters(self, expected: List[str], \n                           provided: Union[List[Any], Dict[str, Any]],\n                           style: ParameterStyle) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Validate that provided parameters match expected.\n        \n        Args:\n            expected: Expected parameter names/positions\n            provided: Provided parameters\n            style: Parameter style\n        \n        Returns:\n            True if valid\n        \n        Raises:\n            ValueError: If validation fails\n        \"\"\"\n        if style == ParameterStyle.QMARK:\n            if not isinstance(provided, (list, tuple)):\n                raise ValueError(\"Positional parameters must be a list or tuple\")\n            if len(provided) != len(expected):\n                raise ValueError(\n                    f\"Parameter count mismatch: expected {len(expected)}, \"\n                    f\"got {len(provided)}\"\n                )\n        else:\n            if not isinstance(provided, dict):\n                raise ValueError(\"Named parameters must be a dictionary\")\n            \n            missing = set(expected) - set(provided.keys())\n            if missing:\n                raise ValueError(f\"Missing parameters: {missing}\")\n            \n            extra = set(provided.keys()) - set(expected)\n            if extra:\n                # Warn about extra parameters but don't fail\n                pass\n        \n        return True\n\n\nclass PreparedStatementCache:\n    \"\"\"\n    Cache for prepared statements with LRU eviction.\n    \n    Thread-safe implementation for concurrent access.\n    \"\"\"\n    \n    def __init__(self, max_size: int = 100):\n        self.max_size = max_size\n        self._cache: OrderedDict[str, PreparedStatement] = OrderedDict()\n        self._lock = threading.RLock()\n        self._stats = {\n            'prepares': 0,\n            'executes': 0,\n            'deallocates': 0,\n            'hits': 0,\n            'misses': 0,\n            'evictions': 0\n        }\n    \n    def prepare(self, name: str, sql: str) -> PreparedStatement:\n        \"\"\"\n        Prepare a statement and add to cache.\n        \n        Args:\n            name: Statement name\n            sql: SQL with parameter placeholders\n        \n        Returns:\n            PreparedStatement object\n        \n        Raises:\n            ValueError: If statement already exists or SQL is invalid\n        \"\"\"\n        with self._lock:\n            if name in self._cache:\n                raise ValueError(f\"Prepared statement already exists: {name}\")\n            \n            # Parse SQL to identify parameters\n            style, params = self._parse_parameters(sql)\n            \n            # Create prepared statement\n            stmt = PreparedStatement(\n                name=name,\n                sql_template=sql,\n                parameter_style=style,\n                parameters=params\n            )\n            \n            # Evict if necessary\n            while len(self._cache) >= self.max_size:\n                self._evict_lru()\n            \n            self._cache[name] = stmt\n            self._stats['prepares'] += 1\n            \n            return stmt\n    \n    def execute(self, name: str, \n                parameters: Union[List[Any], Dict[str, Any]] = None) -> str:\n        \"\"\"\n        Execute a prepared statement with parameters.\n        \n        Args:\n            name: Statement name\n            parameters: Values to bind\n        \n        Returns:\n            SQL with parameters bound\n        \n        Raises:\n            ValueError: If statement not found or parameters invalid\n        \"\"\"\n        with self._lock:\n            stmt = self._cache.get(name)\n            \n            if not stmt:\n                self._stats['misses'] += 1\n                raise ValueError(f\"Prepared statement not found: {name}\")\n            \n            self._stats['hits'] += 1\n            self._stats['executes'] += 1\n            \n            # Move to end (most recently used)\n            self._cache.move_to_end(name)\n            stmt.touch()\n            \n            # Bind parameters\n            binder = ParameterBinder()\n            \n            if parameters is None:\n                parameters = [] if stmt.parameter_style == ParameterStyle.QMARK else {}\n            \n            binder.validate_parameters(stmt.parameters, parameters, stmt.parameter_style)\n            \n            return binder.bind_parameters(\n                stmt.sql_template, \n                parameters, \n                stmt.parameter_style\n            )\n    \n    def deallocate(self, name: str) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Remove a prepared statement from cache.\n        \n        Args:\n            name: Statement name\n        \n        Returns:\n            True if removed, False if not found\n        \"\"\"\n        with self._lock:\n            if name in self._cache:\n                del self._cache[name]\n                self._stats['deallocates'] += 1\n                return True\n            return False\n    \n    def deallocate_all(self):\n        \"\"\"Remove all prepared statements.\"\"\"\n        with self._lock:\n            self._cache.clear()\n            self._stats['deallocates'] += len(self._cache)\n    \n    def get(self, name: str) -> Optional[PreparedStatement]:\n        \"\"\"Get a prepared statement without executing.\"\"\"\n        with self._lock:\n            stmt = self._cache.get(name)\n            if stmt:\n                self._cache.move_to_end(name)\n                stmt.touch()\n            return stmt\n    \n    def _parse_parameters(self, sql: str) -> Tuple[ParameterStyle, List[str]]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Parse SQL to identify parameter style and names.\n        \n        Returns:\n            Tuple of (style, parameter_list)\n        \"\"\"\n        # Check for positional ? markers\n        qmark_count = sql.count('?')\n        if qmark_count > 0:\n            return ParameterStyle.QMARK, list(range(qmark_count))\n        \n        # Check for named :param markers\n        named_params = re.findall(r':([a-zA-Z_][a-zA-Z0-9_]*)', sql)\n        if named_params:\n            return ParameterStyle.NAMED, named_params\n        \n        # Check for Python-style %(name)s markers\n        pyformat_params = re.findall(r'%\\\\(([a-zA-Z_][a-zA-Z0-9_]*)\\\\)s', sql)\n        if pyformat_params:\n            return ParameterStyle.PYFORMAT, pyformat_params\n        \n        # No parameters\n        return ParameterStyle.QMARK, []\n    \n    def _evict_lru(self):\n        \"\"\"Evict least recently used statement.\"\"\"\n        if self._cache:\n            oldest = next(iter(self._cache))\n            del self._cache[oldest]\n            self._stats['evictions'] += 1\n    \n    def get_stats(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        \"\"\"Get cache statistics.\"\"\"\n        with self._lock:\n            return {\n                'size': len(self._cache),\n                'max_size': self.max_size,\n                'prepares': self._stats['prepares'],\n                'executes': self._stats['executes'],\n                'deallocates': self._stats['deallocates'],\n                'hits': self._stats['hits'],\n                'misses': self._stats['misses'],\n                'evictions': self._stats['evictions'],\n                'hit_rate': self._stats['hits'] / (self._stats['hits'] + self._stats['misses'])\n                           if (self._stats['hits'] + self._stats['misses']) > 0 else 0.0\n            }\n    \n    def list_statements(self) -> List[str]:\n        \"\"\"List all prepared statement names.\"\"\"\n        with self._lock:\n            return list(self._cache.keys())\n    \n    def explain(self) -> str:\n        \"\"\"Generate human-readable cache status.\"\"\"\n        stats = self.get_stats()\n        \n        lines = [\n            \"Prepared Statement Cache Status:\",\n            \"=\" * 50,\n            f\"Size: {stats['size']} / {stats['max_size']} statements\",\n            f\"Prepares: {stats['prepares']}\",\n {stats['evictions']}\",\n            \"\",\n            \"Prepared Statements:\",\n            \"-\" * 30\n        ]\n        \n        with self._lock:\n            for name, stmt in {len(stmt.parameters)} params, \"\n                    f\"{stmt.use_count} uses, \"\n                    f\"last_used={last_used:.0f}s ago\"\n                )\n        \n        return \"\\\\n\".join(lines)\n\n\n# SQL Injection Prevention Tests\nclass SQLInjectionTest:\n    \"\"\"\n    Test cases for SQL injection prevention.\n    \"\"\"\n    \n    TEST_CASES = [\n        # (description, template, params, expected_pattern)\n        (\n            \"Basic string\",\n            \"SELECT * FROM users WHERE name = ?\",\n            [\"Alice\"],\n            r\"SELECT \\\\* FROM users WHERE name = 'Alice'\"\n        ),\n        (\n            \"Quote in string\",\n            \"SELECT * FROM users WHERE name = ?\",\n            [\"O'Brien\"],\n            r\"SELECT \\\\* FROM users WHERE name = 'O''Brien'\"\n        ),\n        (\n            \"Double quote in string\",\n            \"SELECT * FROM users WHERE name = ?\",\n            ['Say \"Hello\"'],\n            r\"SELECT \\\\* FROM users WHERE name = 'Say ''Hello'''\"\n        ),\n        (\n            \"Backslash in string\",\n            \"SELECT * FROM users WHERE path = ?\",\n passwords'\"\n        ),\n        (\n            \"Named parameter\",\n            \"SELECT * FROM users WHERE name = :name AND age > :min_age\",\n            {\"name\": \"Alice\", \"min_age\": 18},\n            r\"SELECT \\\\* FROM users WHERE name = 'Alice' AND age > 18\"\n        ),\n        (\n            \"Integer parameter\",\n            \"SELECT * FROM users WHERE id = ?\",\n            [42],\n            r\"SELECT \\\\* FROM users WHERE id = 42\"\n        ),\n        (\n            \"Float parameter\",\n            \"SELECT * FROM products WHERE price = ?\",\n            [19.99],\n            r\"SELECT \\\\* FROM products WHERE price = 19\\\\.99\"\n        ),\n        (\n            \"Boolean parameter\",\n            \"SELECT * FROM users WHERE active = ?\",\n            [True],\n            r\"SELECT \\\\* FROM users WHERE active = TRUE\"\n        ),\n        (\n            \"NULL parameter\",\n            \"SELECT * FROM users WHERE deleted_at = ?\",\n            [None],\n            r\"SELECT \\\\* FROM users WHERE deleted_at = NULL\"\n        ),\n    ]\n    \n    @classmethod\n    def run_tests(cls) -> List[Tuple[str, bool, str]]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Run all SQL injection test cases.\n        \n        Returns:\n            List of (description, passed, message) tuples\n        \"\"\"\n        results = []\n        binder = ParameterBinder()\n        \n        for desc, template, params, expected_pattern in cls.TEST_CASES:\n            try:\n                if isinstance(params, dict):\n                    sql = binder.bind_named(template, params)\n                else:\n                    sql = binder.bind_positional(template, params)\n                \n                import re as regex\n                if regex.search(expected_pattern, sql):\n                    results.append((desc, True, \"Passed\"))\n                else:\n                    results.append((desc, False, f\"Pattern mismatch. Got: {sql}\"))\n            except Exception as e:\n                results.append((desc, False, str(e)))\n        \n        return results\n\n\n# Convenience functions\ndef create_prepared_cache(max_size: int = 100) -> PreparedStatementCache:\n    \"\"\"Create a prepared statement cache.\"\"\"\n    return PreparedStatementCache(max_size=max_size)\n\n\ndef prepare_statement(cache: PreparedStatementCache, \n                      name: str, \n                      sql: str) -> PreparedStatement:\n    \"\"\"Prepare a statement.\"\"\"\n    return cache.prepare(name, sql)\n\n\ndef execute_statement(cache: PreparedStatementCache,\n                      name: str,\n                      parameters: Union[List[Any], Dict[str, Any]] = None) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Execute a prepared statement.\"\"\"\n    return cache.execute(name, parameters)\n\n\n# Example usage\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    #
